Martyr Fan Hongxian's Coffin Will Be Transported to Beijing Tomorrow 90

Will be buried in the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen on January 3rd next year.

The late General Fan Hongxian, who died for his country, was temporarily buried in Shanghai in the third year of the Republic of China. The Central Government, in commemoration of his past merits, issued an order to commend him and posthumously conferred him the rank of General, and had him buried in the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen to show the nation's respect for loyalty and martyrdom. It appointed committee members Li Zhengqiu and others to prepare the funeral. The funeral date was set for January 3rd next year. Li and others came to Shanghai the night before yesterday and decided to transport the coffin to Beijing tomorrow (22nd). Details are listed below.

A Brief Biography of Fan Hongxian

Martyr Fan Hongxian, also known as Guangqi, was from Hefei County, Anhui Province. He was fond of learning from a young age and was known in the world for his writing. Before the Xinhai Revolution, he and Song Jiaoren, Yu Youren and others advocated revolution with their writing. At that time, literati from home and abroad responded to him. When he was in charge of the People’s Voice, Dr. Sun Yat-Sen once said to Fan Hongxian, "Your pen can sweep away hundreds of thousands of soldiers." Fan Hongxian’s contribution to the overthrow of the Qing Dynasty was significant. In the first year of the Republic of China, he served in the Iron Blood Army. His contribution to the Battle of Nanjing was especially great. When the North and South reached an agreement, he retired to Shanghai and wrote articles to rectify his comrades. When Yuan Shikai stole the country, Fan Hongxian, in order to fulfill his original revolutionary intention, launched another uprising to denounce and punish him, repeatedly defeating the bandits and pacifying Jianghuai. After the GuiChou Incident, he was ordered by Dr. Sun Yat-Sen to co-lead the Shanghai Revolutionary Military with Chen Qimei. Yuan Shikai was afraid of his name and increased the intensity of his capture. In the third year of the Republic of China, he was assassinated by Ren Suo and died for his country. In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, the capital was established in Nanjing. The Central Government, in commemoration of the martyr’s past merits, appointed Zhang Jingjiang and others to submit a special proposal to the Central Government, issued an order to commend him, posthumously conferred him the rank of General, and had him buried in the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen, and ordered the formation of a funeral preparation committee to be responsible for handling the funeral to show loyalty and martyrdom, and increased the funeral expenses. His life deeds were submitted to the Party History. Committee members Wu Zhijing, Jin Weixi, Liu Wendian, Li Zhengqiu, Zhang Gongchen, Wang Juemin, Yin Zhilu, Xuan Yujie, Wei Lihuang, Fan Xuejun, and others were appointed as funeral preparation committee members. After a long period of preparation, they were able to complete the task and decided to welcome the spirit to Beijing for burial tomorrow to show the loyal soul.

The Coffin Moves to Beijing

The special commissioner for welcoming the coffin came to Shanghai the night before yesterday and decided to hold the coffin raising ceremony at the Anhui Funeral Home in Rihui Port at 1:00 PM tomorrow. A public memorial service will be held at the North Station at 4:00 PM, and the coffin will be moved to Beijing. Li and others specially hosted a reception for people from all walks of life at the Youth Association Building on Baxianqiao at 6:00 PM last night, including Fan Hongxian's old friends Xu Shiying, Ding Fubao, Guan Yunnong, Gao Jitang, Li Yuanzhu, and party, government, and military representatives Tong Hangbai (representing Huang E), Li Dachao, Wang Zhinan, and more than 30 reporters from various newspapers. Li Zhengqiu presided over the meeting and reported on the progress of the funeral preparations. Gong Zhenpeng reported on Martyr Fan's life deeds. The meeting ended at 7:00 PM.

Funeral Preparations

Li Zhengqiu reported on the funeral preparations, saying that Mr. Fan Hongxian, a martyr from Anhui, was assassinated in Shanghai in the third year of the Republic of China by Yuan Shikai's agents. His coffin was temporarily placed in Shanghai and has not been properly buried to this day. In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, the Central Government issued an order to commend him, citing the example of Martyr Liao Zhongkai, and had him buried in the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen, allocated funeral expenses, and built a tomb. His life deeds were submitted to the Party History. At the same time, Wu Zhijing, Jin Weixi, Liu Wendian, Zhang Gongchen, Wang Juemin, Yin Zhilu, Xuan Yujie, Tan Shanwu, Wei Lihuang, Li Zhengqiu, Fan Xuejun, and other comrades were appointed as members of the funeral preparation committee and established a funeral preparation committee in Nanjing to carry out preparations. The Central Government was requested to demarcate the address in the eastern area of the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen. The land had beautiful mountains, rivers, forests, and excellent scenery. Chen Zhulin, a famous architect from Shanghai, and Yin Zhilu, an engineer from the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, were hired to design the building, including the tomb hall and pavilion. Inscriptions and memoirs were written by famous party and state figures. Construction began, and it took several years to complete. It is magnificent, quiet and beautiful, and祭Enjoy and commemoration are sufficient to encourage future generations. A meeting was held on the 17th of this month and resolved: (1) The burial date will be January 3, 1936. The date of welcoming the spirit will be this month's 22nd. Zhang Gongchen, Yin Zhilu, and Li Zhengqiu, members of the preparatory committee, were publicly nominated as special commissioners to welcome the coffin to Shanghai. (2) Welcoming the spirit to Beijing should be divided into four groups: general affairs, document, reception, and ceremony, each responsible for its duties. Jin Mengkui, Gong Jinyi, and Zhao Huasan were appointed to the general affairs group; Zhao Zishu, Shi Keshi, Hong Guannan, Li Shanchou, and Jiang Lisheng to the document group; Chen Baozhi, Han Chuangzhi, and Ni Damin to the reception group; Xiao Qin and Chen Yin'nan to the ceremony group. (3) The Central Government was requested to notify the party and government agencies in Beijing and Shanghai to send personnel to participate in the coffin raising ceremony, the welcoming of the spirit, and the memorial service, and the Ministry of Railways to prepare a train to transport the spirit. (4) The Martyrs' Shrine of the First Park in Nanjing was used as the place to stop the spirit. (5) Committee member Jin Weixi and Committee member Wang Juemin were publicly elected to take charge of the welcoming affairs in Nanjing, and Wu Zhijing to take charge of accounting affairs. The coffin raising ceremony is scheduled to be held at the Anhui Funeral Home in Rihui Port (south of Panjia Wooden Bridge at the end of Jin Shenfu Road) at 1:00 PM on the 22nd of this month. At 4:00 PM, a public memorial service will be held at the North Station. After the memorial service, the spirit will be transported to Beijing. The departure route has been separately announced by this association in the newspaper. The comrades were dispatched to Shanghai yesterday and only had three days to prepare. In such a short time, it was so grand.

Party and Government Notice

The Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government, in order to mourn Mr. Fan Hongxian's loyal deeds, have issued a notice to all agencies and groups in the city to send representatives to participate in the funeral and public memorial service. The original text is as follows: Mr. Fan Hongxian's coffin has been approved by the Central Government to be buried in the attached area of ​​the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen, and it is scheduled to be transported from the Anhui Hall in Rihui Port to the North Railway Station at 2:00 PM on the 22nd of this month. A public memorial service will be held at the North Station at 4:00 PM, and a night train will be used to transport it to Beijing at 11:00 PM. In addition to having sent separate letters to all agencies and groups in the city to send representatives to participate in the funeral and public memorial service, a special notice is hereby issued.

Anti-Smoking Propaganda Scheduled for Ten Days Starting Yesterday 91

The Anti-Smoking Committee releases pamphlets for smokers to pay attention to.

According to the Central News Agency, the anti-smoking work in the city has been actively carried out since the establishment of the Anti-Smoking Committee. Recently, the committee has entered the period of compulsory registration for anti-smoking, so on the 17th, it held an open-air lecture with the Public Security Bureau to persuade smokers to surrender as soon as possible to avoid arrest and severe punishment. The committee believes that it is still necessary to continue to hold official propaganda to expand its reach. Therefore, it has reorganized the propaganda team and set off on different routes to give lectures starting yesterday (20th), while distributing pamphlets to promote smokers' awareness. It is reported that the committee has decided to set a period of ten days. The propaganda locations are: Nanshi on the first day, Pudong on the second day, Xinzha on the third day, North Station on the fourth day, West Gate on the fifth day, Jiangwan on the sixth day, Old North Gate on the seventh day, Huxi on the eighth day, Gaoqiao on the ninth day, and Zhenru on the tenth day. The pamphlet "Smokers' Attention" issued by the committee is attached below. It is hoped that smokers in the city will pay attention: "The anti-smoking work has now shifted from voluntary registration to compulsory registration. However, according to the Public Security Bureau's report, as of now, only 27,000 to 8,000 smokers have registered. However, the city has a large population, and there are definitely more than this number of smokers. As it looks, there are still many, many smokers who have not registered. Originally, during this compulsory registration period, the committee would urge the Public Security Bureau to strictly investigate and arrest those who have not registered and impose a fine of 50 yuan to 300 yuan in accordance with the law, and then order them to register. There is no possibility of voluntary registration. But among these unregistered smokers, there are undoubtedly some who are cunning and play tricks, but there are also many who are ignorant and foolish. Therefore, the Municipal Government is giving you smokers another way to rehabilitate, a flexible approach that allows you to surrender during this compulsory registration period. All smokers who have not registered can go to the city's Public Security Bureau or its subordinate branches to request registration within the recent period, and they will still be treated the same as voluntary registration and will not be punished. Also, those who want to quit smoking for free can also rest assured and quickly register. This opportunity is running out of time. You smokers must not make another mistake. If you still want to try to evade and delay your surrender, you will be punished in accordance with the law when the Public Security Bureau finds out or is reported by someone, and you will not be tolerated. The above-mentioned method of allowing surrender has been announced by the Public Security Bureau. The committee is sincerely afraid that you smokers will still overlook it, so it has specially reorganized the propaganda team to publicize it as much as possible and distribute this leaflet to make you all aware of this method and the harm of further delay, so as to avoid the government regretting punishing without teaching. It is hoped that you smokers will appreciate the committee's painstaking efforts, abide by the government's laws, quickly turn over a new leaf, and surrender and register. Do not test the law with your own bodies and regret it! Also, those of you who sell private opium, open smoking dens, and use licenses to allow people to smoke, should quickly become aware and find other legitimate businesses, because now the government, in order to completely ban the conversion, has made this law very strict. From today onwards, the city's Public Security Bureau has been supervising its subordinate branches to conduct strict searches. Once discovered, they will be sent to the Garrison Headquarters and punished according to military law, and will not be lenient at all. It is hoped that you will not seek these small profits and suffer severe punishments. This is also the committee's very sincere advice to you. It is hoped that you will pay special attention. Shanghai Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee"

Establishment of a Hospital for Quitting Smoking Plan 92

A Document Submitted to the Municipal Government by Two Bureaus

The New Voice Society reports: The Public Security and Public Health Bureaus are working extremely hard on the matter of establishing a hospital for quitting smoking. They are currently jointly submitting a document to the municipal government. The detailed plan for establishing the hospital is recorded below. The case is based on Instruction No. 3387 from your office, stating that according to a report from the Public Security Bureau, the number of arrested smokers has increased during the period of mandatory registration. All existing hospitals for quitting smoking are unable to accommodate them. Please instruct the Public Health Bureau to jointly prepare and report on the establishment of a temporary hospital capable of accommodating 500 people. Having received this instruction, this bureau found that there are over 4,000 people who have voluntarily requested to quit smoking to the Public Security Bureau. Apart from the 1,738 people who have already been sent for treatment, there are still over 2,000 people waiting to be sent. In addition, with the current mandatory registration, dozens of people are being ordered to quit smoking every day. Apart from the 50 beds that have already been added to the existing Shanghai North Quitting Smoking Hospital by this Public Health Bureau using existing funds, which has been reported in a separate document, the establishment of a temporary hospital with 500 beds is indeed necessary to meet the urgent need. However, opening a hospital with 500 beds will inevitably require considerable housing. After joint discussion, it was found that only the houses in the Gaoging Temple Memorial Village are suitable for renovation and use. According to preliminary estimates, the renovation cost will be approximately 5,830 yuan, and the cost of connecting water and electricity will be 3,300 yuan. However, the houses in the Memorial Village are the property of the Shanghai Municipal Local Association. It is now proposed to borrow them for a short period. Please request the Local Association to transfer a portion of the houses that were previously borrowed from the Association by the Social Bureau to be temporarily allocated for our use. They will be returned after the hospital is closed. The duration of the temporary hospital's existence is estimated to be about three to four months, based on the number of smokers registered by the Public Security Bureau. Therefore, the treatment for temporary staff must be appropriately increased to encourage diligent service. To save expenses, it is proposed to request the allocation of the iron beds currently stored in the Municipal Sports Ground for use. This will reduce the purchase cost by 20,344 yuan. The cost of medical equipment and medicines will also be reduced by finding ways to transfer existing supplies, requiring only an opening cost of 2,000 yuan. Therefore, the total opening cost is only 21,474 yuan. Moreover, due to the remote location, security must be taken seriously. It is proposed that the Public Security Bureau allocate a squad from the Police Corps to be stationed permanently to ensure safety and to encourage those undergoing treatment to engage in light gardening work to exercise and benefit their physical and mental health. The total monthly operating expense is 11,446 yuan. The above requirements are intended to be as economical as possible, with no room for further savings. If approved, we will begin preparations immediately to facilitate smoking cessation. We hereby submit a detailed budget for your review and approval. Please grant the allocation quickly, so that preparations can be completed within the month and the hospital can be opened as soon as possible for the public good. Respectfully submitted by Mayor Wu.

Inauguration of the National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau Yesterday 94

Another Management Committee Will Be Formed to Supervise Production and Sales; Branch Sales Offices Will Be Established in Various Locations for Local Distribution

The Central News Agency reports: The National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau, supervised by the Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior, was officially established in Shanghai yesterday. The Management Committee convened at noon to discuss its progress. It is planned to manufacture two million flags by the end of the year for nationwide display on New Year's Day. The opening date is yet to be determined. Details are noted below:

Established Yesterday

The Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior, to coordinate the management of the national flag, previously solicited bids from merchants to manufacture the national flag. After investigation and review, the Shanghai Textile Printing and Dyeing Company and the China Flag Manufacturing Company were selected as the manufacturers. Representatives from the two companies were convened in Beijing for a meeting, where it was decided that the two companies would jointly establish the National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau. The organizational outline has been approved by the Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior, and special commissioners have been appointed to supervise and guide it. The bureau is located at No. 30 Jiyi Lane, Nanjing Road. Yesterday marked the bureau's establishment. The Central Propaganda Department sent Liu Derong, and the Ministry of Interior sent Li An to Shanghai to guide all matters. A first Management Committee meeting was held yesterday afternoon to draft various procedures and set a date for the opening. It was also decided to manufacture two million flags of ten different sizes and styles by the end of the year, all in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the central government. The flags must also be stamped to ensure uniformity.

Organizational Outline

Article 1 of the National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau's organizational outline states that the bureau is organized by the national flag manufacturing shops permitted by the Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior. The currently permitted manufacturing shops are the Shanghai Textile Printing and Dyeing Company and the China Flag Manufacturing Company. Article 2 states that the two companies organizing the bureau in the previous article are independent of each other internally. If a company is unwilling or unable to manufacture and withdraws from the bureau, the other manufacturer must continue to operate. Article 3 states that the bureau is under the guidance and supervision of the Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior. Each company shall appoint three representatives to form a Management Committee to oversee all manufacturing and sales matters. Article 4 states that the Management Committee shall establish two standing committee members to handle daily affairs, who shall be mutually elected by the committee. Article 5 states that the bureau shall establish four sections: General Affairs, Design, Manufacturing Verification, and Distribution, each with a director and several staff members, who shall be responsible for their respective tasks under the direction of the standing committee members. The staff of each section shall be appointed or hired by the Management Committee. Article 6 states that the bureau may appoint technicians as deemed appropriate by the Management Committee to improve flag manufacturing technology and to be responsible for technical design and research. Article 7 states that in order to facilitate guidance and supervision of all bureau activities, the Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior shall each send a commissioner to the bureau to handle affairs. Article 8 states that the Management Committee shall meet at least once a month. In the event of a tie vote, the decision shall be made by the supervising commissioner sent by the central government. Article 9 states that all expenses of the bureau shall be borne equally by the two companies. Article 10 states that the bureau shall be located in Shanghai and may establish branch sales offices in various provinces, cities, and counties for local distribution. Article 11 states that this outline shall be implemented upon approval by the Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior.

Conversation with Wang Yingbin, Secretary of the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department 95

The Progress of Cotton Industry Promotion in Zhejiang Province (Continued)

Estimated Quantity of Seed Purchase

Practically speaking, we only need to take the quantity of improved seed cotton already collected at the flower collection stations in each implementation area to understand everything. For clarity, we can provide a statistical overview of the quantity already purchased, the estimated quantity, and the quantity yet to be collected.

Area: Quantity Already Purchased Estimated Quantity Not Yet Collected

Dinghai: 75,300 catties

Hang County: 132,160 catties 10,000 catties

Cixi: 1,574,30 catties 196,780 catties

Yin County: 2,990 catties 22,000 catties

Yuyao Seed Cotton Lint Cotton 1,210,584 catties 10,144 catties 800,000 catties

Improved Cotton Seeds are of Excellent Quality

Mr. Wang also said that the improved cotton produced in each improved cotton industry implementation area has been analyzed in detail, and its quality is excellent, and the fiber is long. This office sent the improved cotton from Dinghai and the local cotton from the surrounding areas to the Agricultural Crop Inspection Office of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry for inspection. According to the inspection results, the improved American cotton seeds can spin 30-count yarn, while the local cotton seeds can only spin 14-count coarse yarn. This clearly demonstrates that the improved cotton seeds are superior to the local cotton. Other areas' improved cotton is undoubtedly superior to local cotton. We have now instructed each area to send improved cotton to the bureau for separate inspections.

Funds Raised by Various Districts for Flower Collection

Mr. Zhu also said that in the early years, for the cotton production of each implementation area, the government originally intended to raise huge sums of money to establish factories jointly by various cooperative societies to centrally collect and sell all cotton. At that time, an operating plan and budget were already drafted and sent to Director Zeng for approval. The total funds required amounted to 1.5 million yuan, and it was decided to borrow from the China Construction Banking Group in Shanghai. I was tasked with contacting the relevant authorities at various banks for consultation, but due to the silver problem at the time, credit was extremely tight, and the loan was not successful. As a result, we had to change our approach. Since the necessary funds could not be borrowed successfully, the plan to establish factories for centralized collection and sales could not be realized. Instead, we reduced the scope and proceeded separately in each area, so that the flower collection could continue. Each district borrowed money to purchase the cotton produced. The loan and flower collection situation in each district can be summarized as follows:

Hang County: Hang County borrowed 40,000 yuan in working capital from the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank, which was used by the cooperative to organize a joint flower collection station.

Xiaoshan: Xiaoshan borrowed 50,000 yuan in working capital from the Jiaotong Bank's Hangzhou branch, which was used by the cooperative to organize a joint flower collection station.

Haiyan: Haiyan borrowed 20,000 yuan from the local bank, which was used by the implementation area to establish a flower collection station. Yuyao: Yuyao borrowed 60,000 yuan in working capital from the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank and the Yuyao Farmers Bank, which was used by the cooperative to organize a joint flower collection station. The American cotton produced in the Xinpu area was approved to be collected by the designated flower merchant Hengfeng Hao.

A Glimpse into the Prosperity and Decline of the Yangtze River Shipping Industry 98

Both Cargo and Passenger Traffic on the Yangtze River Decline; Ten More New Ships Added to the Sichuan Route

Recently, the Yangtze River shipping industry has experienced changes. Both cargo and passenger traffic have decreased. However, on the Sichuan route, a large number of new ships have been added. Details are listed below:

Cessation of Grain Transport

The transport of miscellaneous grains from Jiujiang and Hankou to Shanghai is the largest source of cargo for various ports along the Yangtze River. Starting from the 15th of this month, a certain number of Shanghai grain and miscellaneous goods businesses suddenly telegraphed Xun and Han ports, instructing them to stop transporting purchased grains to Shanghai. Jiujiang, Hankou, and other ports have not shipped grains since last Friday, causing a significant reduction in imported goods arriving in Shanghai on the Yangtze River downriver ships of various companies in recent days. Even the ships traveling to Nanhua and other places have suffered related losses. Transportation is slow, and business is declining.

Passenger Traffic Declines

All nine of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River ships, except for the Jiangjing, still operate under the revenue guarantee system for business directors. The China Merchants ships have always focused on passenger traffic, so the Jianghua, Jiangshun, Jiang'an, and Jiangxin ships are all listed as first-class ships. Recently, passenger traffic on all Yangtze River ports, both upriver and downriver, has declined to an extreme degree. Because of the revenue guarantee system within the company, it is not responsible for the success or failure of passenger ticket sales. Consequently, the business directors of each Yangtze River ship have suffered significant losses due to the slow business, making it difficult to sustain. As a result of collective discussions, all of the business directors of the Yangtze River ships have jointly submitted a request to the head office to reduce the monthly revenue guarantee fee, based on the current period, by one hundred.

Inspection of the Shipping Industry

Gao Tingzi, Director of the Shipping Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications, is inspecting the Yangtze River shipping industry to revive the national shipping industry. Therefore, on the 15th, he first went to the Nanjing branch of the China Merchants Bureau to inspect and give instructions, and then went to Wuhu for inspection. This station received a telegram yesterday that Director Gao had taken the Jiangxin ship to Anqing to inspect the shipping administration in central Anhui. He is scheduled to transfer to the Jiang'an ship today to go to Jiujiang, pass through Hankou, and go to Shashi and Yichang to thoroughly investigate the status of the Yangtze River shipping industry in its entirety to provide a basis for planning the revival of the national shipping industry on the Yangtze River.

Significant Increase in Sichuan Ships

This autumn, the Sichuan River ships' business is better than usual. The income of each ship at its highest level is about twelve to fifteen times higher, which is rarely seen. The profits of the Minsheng Company are especially huge, and the cost of purchasing the Jijiang ships has already been recovered. Now, due to the scarcity of ships caused by the abundance of goods and the soaring shipping fees, the company is urgently adding and purchasing eight new ships for expansion. The following can be launched and operated by the end of this month: (1) The Minxing ship, which is being built by the Hexing Shipyard; and the following will be completed by the end of the year: (2) The Minyun ship and (3) the Xinminkang ship, both built by the Jiangnan Shipyard. In addition, (4) the Minxi ship, (5) the Minlai ship, (6) the Minsu ship, (7) the Minshi ship, and (8) the Minting ship are also being rushed to be launched from the dock and operated within these four to five months. Furthermore, the Mintai and Minju ships will be converted into barges dedicated to transporting tung oil and miscellaneous goods. After this, the number of Minsheng ships operating on the Sichuan River will reach more than fifty. The number of ships suddenly increased by sixteen or seventeen in the autumn and winter of this year. The situation created is indeed unexpected. According to people in the shipping industry, if the China Merchants Bureau had purchased the Jijiang ships at that time and operated them until today, the shipping fees would have already earned about four million yuan.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Indicates Stamp Tax Should be Paid on Rent Books 110

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to Laochengfeng Company yesterday regarding the stamp tax that should be paid on rent books, stating: We are responding to your letter of inquiry of the 19th of this month regarding whether or not stamp tax should be paid on rent books. According to the so-called rent book in your letter, it is a rental document contract in Article 16, Section 10 of the Stamp Tax Law. The tax rate in the section has been stipulated. If a rent book is used to collect rent, stamp tax of two jiao per item per year should be paid according to the example of the fourth item of the same article. The so-called collection of rent in the letter is in accordance with the nature column, which states that all documents and contracts related to the rental of various movable or immovable properties and leased land are applicable. Therefore, whether it is a house rent book or a field rent book, stamp tax should be paid in accordance with the law. Your letter refers to Section 11 of the same article, stating that it is not for business use, but it does not take into account Section 10 of the same article, which is a misunderstanding.

Knitting Industry Association Establishes a Product Evaluation Committee 111

To facilitate the rectification of products and prices among fellow members of the knitting industry, the Knitting Industry Association has established product evaluation committees for each category of member products, including sock group, underwear group, outerwear group, glove group, and towel, hat, and band group. The organizational outline is recorded as follows: Article 1. This outline is formulated based on Article 4 of the industry regulations. Article 2. This committee establishes the following groups based on the category of products of fellow members: (1) Sock Group Product Evaluation Committee, including yarn, thread, wool, silk, and interwoven types from "power machine shares" and "manual machine shares." (2) Underwear Group Product Evaluation Committee, including weaving types from "cotton weaving shares," "hand weaving shares," "silk weaving shares," and "interwoven shares." (3) Outerwear Group Product Evaluation Committee, including weaving types from "cotton weaving shares," "wool weaving shares," "silk weaving shares," and "interwoven shares." (4) Handicraft Group Product Evaluation Committee, including weaving types from "cotton weaving shares," "wool weaving shares," "silk total shares," and "interwoven shares." (5) Towel, Hat, and Band Group Product Evaluation Committee, including weaving types from "cotton weaving shares," "wool weaving shares," "silk weaving shares," and "interwoven shares." Article 3. If it is necessary to add any committees in addition to the committees mentioned in the previous article, the executive committee of this association may decide to add them. Article 4. The method of producing committee members mentioned in the previous paragraph is based on the members of each group as the standard. If there are more than three members in the same group, two committee members may be mutually elected. In addition, one committee member may be added for every three additional members, and one director shall be elected. Each group shall submit the list to the executive committee of this association for filing. Article 5. In order to concentrate and refine discussions, each group committee may convene meetings of members of the same share and category. The results of the meeting shall be passed by each group committee and copied to the executive committee of this association for review and execution. Article 6. The duties of each group committee are as follows: (1) To check the cost of each item and set the price. (2) To review the products of each factory and formulate grade standards. Article 7. The affairs discussed by each committee or the same share and category committee shall be decided by a majority of the attendees and with the consent of a majority of the attendees. Article 8. The matters decided by each committee shall be submitted to the executive committee of this association for review and execution. Article 9. Each committee shall be convened by the chairman for each meeting. In case of special circumstances, a temporary meeting may be convened. Article 10. If there are any matters not covered in this outline, the executive committee may revise them. Article 11. This outline shall be implemented by the executive committee.

Guangdong Provincial Bank Employee Embezzles Huge Sum and Flees to Shanghai 119

Hiding with Mistress in De Lin Apartment - Detained by Police and Remanded for Further Questioning

Yang Peter, a native of Guangdong, 32 years old, was an employee in the vault of the Guangdong Bank in Hong Kong. In August of the year before last, he embezzled more than 198,000 yuan from the bank and fled without a trace. The bank reported it to the Hong Kong government, which issued Arrest Warrant No. 18 on August 15, 1931, offering a reward for his arrest. Yang, using the alias Peter, came to Shanghai and stayed, keeping his whereabouts secret and living freely. Recently, he hid with his mistress Wang Baoqiong (also from Guangdong) in Room 242 of the De Lin Apartment on Chongming Road. The bank found out and telegraphed the Hongkou Police Department. At 8:00 a.m. the day before yesterday, Chinese Detective Zheng Zulin and Western Detective K. Kopple went to the address and arrested him. Three leather suitcases were found in the room, containing more than a hundred pieces of men's and women's clothing, as well as a Citibank deposit receipt for 1,000 yuan, Hong Kong banknotes and silver coins, and Chinese currency totaling more than 300 yuan. There were quite a few gold ornaments, jade articles, and jewels. He and Wang were taken to the police station. After questioning, it was found that Gan Baoqiong was not involved in the case and was released. Yang was taken into custody. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Criminal Division 1 of the First Special District Court. Li Zhishan, the lawyer of the Public Works Department, recounted the incident and requested that he be detained to consider the issue of jurisdiction and whether the Hong Kong authorities would extradite him, with a postponement of ten days. When questioned, Yang Peter confessed that the above-mentioned sum was not embezzled, but was a loan released through his hands. Yan Jiangyi, a lawyer, defended him. Judge Su Xiexun ordered him to be remanded in custody and rescheduled for further verification.

General Arrangement

Japanese Forges Naval Documents to Swindle Huge Sums from Chinese Merchants 123

According to the Japanese "Shanghai Daily," Keijiro Fujinuma, a resident of Tokyo residing at No. 14, Lane 81, Kunshan Road, colluded with his fellow broker Tomoyoshi Takeuchi to forge Japanese naval documents to secretly transport 200 boxes of rayon, totaling 4 million pounds worth more than 67,000 yuan, to swindle a huge sum of money from Chinese merchants. The case has been completely exposed. The Japanese Consulate General announced the following on the evening of the 19th: Last December, a Chinese merchant Xu Pizhang entrusted a Japanese broker Takeuchi to secretly transport rayon. Takeuchi had previously served as an interpreter in the Japanese Army. Xu did not know that he had been dismissed, and Takeuchi also falsely claimed that he was still serving as a secretary and interpreter in the Marine Corps Headquarters, and said that he could obtain a transportation permit from the Ministry of the Navy. Xu believed it to be true, so last December, he invited several Chinese capitalists, including Zhou Jingru, to the Zhonghui Building to meet with Takeuchi and Fujinuma. Zhou Jingru sent a representative Zhou Huizhao to negotiate and order 200 boxes of rayon. Fujinuma agreed with Zhou to pay 34,000 yuan in foreign currency. After the rayon arrived in Shanghai, it was agreed that each box would be given to Takeuchi and Fujinuma as a reward of 30 yuan. Takeuchi and Fujinuma then proceeded to forge naval documents, "Japanese Navy Permit." Takeuchi also obtained 800 yuan from Xu Pizhang in the name of travel expenses and lobbying fees, and took his mistress Masako Tamaya to Japan. Fujinuma also obtained 100 yuan from Xu for travel expenses, and went to Japan with Xu's agent Gu Guxiang. They met with Takeuchi in Kyoto. After Gu obtained the permit from Takeuchi, he telegraphed Xu Pizhang in Shanghai to remit the money. Xu remitted 38,880 yuan from the Yokohama Specie Bank in Shanghai. Takeuchi claimed to prepare for the transportation of goods and travel expenses, obtained 6,000 yuan, and spent it lavishly with Fujinuma. Half of the rayon was sold off in Dalian, leaving only 10,000 pounds, which were transported to Shanghai by the Liangzhou Maru. The 18,000 yuan of money sold in Dalian was distributed jointly, with Fujinuma getting more than 7,000 yuan and Takeuchi more than 5,000 yuan. Unexpectedly, when the Liangzhou Maru arrived in Shanghai, it was discovered by the Customs, and the matter was exposed. The Japanese Consulate has investigated the case and sentenced Fujinuma to two years in prison and Takeuchi to two years and six months.

Letter from the Tobacco Exchange Guild to the Money Exchange Guild: Request to Investigate the “Guangjiao” Black Market Rate 127

The Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Guild sent a letter to the Money Exchange Guild yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Money Exchange Guild: Upon receiving your letter stating that, following orders, the exchange rate for subsidiary coins should be fixed at 12 "jiao" per yuan from November 4th, with no increases or decreases allowed, we immediately notified all members to comply. However, the recent fluctuations in exchange rates have caused misunderstandings among outsiders, who believe that tobacco exchange shops are manipulating the market and creating chaos. Therefore, we convened a joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members on the afternoon of the 19th of this month to discuss 'What is the root cause of the current discrepancies in exchange rates, and how should this be thoroughly investigated?' According to reports from various members, the daily money market quotations specify an exchange rate of 12 "jiao" for subsidiary coins. However, the 'Shanghai Business Voice Daily' (also known as the "Foreign Cent Sheet") published on November 19th listed a "Guangjiao" black market rate of '11 "jiao" and 1 "li"'. Tobacco exchange shops exchange one yuan of legal tender for 11 "jiao" and 1 "li" from various money exchange shops. This is equivalent to 10 "jiao" in small silver coins and 25 copper coins, which is in line with the "Guangjiao" black market rate. Therefore, each yuan of legal tender exchanged for 10 "jiao" and 25 copper coins leaves no profit for tobacco exchange shops, making it clear that there is no manipulation or chaos. The "Guangjiao" black market rate on the "Foreign Cent Sheet" is puzzling. We request the Money Exchange Guild to investigate and respond to clarify the situation." The records have been documented. Enclosed are two copies of the "Foreign Cent Sheet" from November 19th and 20th. We hope that your guild will investigate and respond accordingly."

Rong Zongjing Discusses the Market Conditions of Flour and Cotton Yarn 128

According to the Central News Agency, the prices of Japanese-made flour and cotton yarn have risen, showing some improvement. Yesterday, a reporter interviewed Rong Zongjing, a leading figure in these industries. His remarks are as follows:

Flour

"My factories, including Shenxin, Maoxin, and Fuxin, had previously suspended operations entirely due to a shortage of raw materials. They have now gradually resumed operations, but work remains intermittent due to raw materials and sales issues. The current flour market is more expensive than in the past, due to the fact that wheat from various regions has been sold out, leading to a shortage of raw materials and rising flour prices. Consequently, the factories' work schedules are constantly uncertain. Previously, this port could sell 3.5 million (units), but now only half of that can be sold, effectively reducing sales. Furthermore, due to cost considerations, foreign raw materials are not being imported. Recently, the market has declined, and rice is cheaper than flour."

Cotton Yarn

"Regarding cotton yarn, the floods in various regions this year have also reduced production compared to the past. Many Chinese-owned yarn factories have suspended operations. Although the market price has risen by 20 yuan compared to the past, they are still struggling to survive. Regarding the resumption of operations at Shenxin Factories 2 and 3, although unemployed workers are in dire need of relief, the environment restricts any possible solutions. The yarn market is in decline and cannot be sustained. As for rumors that the Ministry of Industry will send personnel to help with the resumption of operations, I have not heard anything about it."

Chuan Shengmao Talks About Chemical Silver Not Being Suitable for Handmade Products 129

Requires a Minimum of 70% Silver Bars

According to Guowen News Agency, although silversmiths have expressed dissatisfaction with the silver usage regulations, the Ministry of Finance believes that the plans have been finalized and cannot be changed. Furthermore, yesterday's newspaper carried a dispatch from Nanjing, stating that a responsible person from the Ministry of Finance believes that the silver usage management rules for silver products were decided after expert research and that some parts follow American precedents. In response, the reporter interviewed Chuan Shengmao, from the Shanghai Silversmiths Guild. According to him, "The silver usage rules for silver products announced by the Ministry of Finance are indeed based on American methods. However, the United States uses machine manufacturing, so the hardness of the silver does not have an impact. China uses handcrafting and has always used pure silver. If we switch to chemical silver, all existing tools will have to be replaced. Furthermore, chemical silver has a poor color and will result in rough and unsightly utensils. This will inevitably affect the business of silversmiths. The current opinion of silversmiths in Shanghai is to request the government to allow the use of 88 silver bars (i.e., 88 taels of silver per 100 taels). At the very least, they should be allowed to use silver bars containing 70% silver; otherwise, the silversmiths' business cannot be sustained."

Distinguishing a Child's Crying Voice: It's the Previous Tenant's Son 130

Investigation the Next Morning Confirms it: The New Tenant is a Child Trafficker

Wang Jiandong, a 33-year-old man from Hangzhou, and Wang Wu, a 37-year-old woman from Huzhou, claiming to be husband and wife, rented a back room on the second floor of No. 2 Hengqing Lane, Belle Road in the French Concession, on the morning of the 11th of this month. They agreed with the sub-landlord, Yang Shuncai, on a monthly rent of 5 yuan. That afternoon, Wang and his wife moved in with a child of about five years old. Little did people know, Wang and his wife were not engaged in legitimate work, but were child traffickers, specializing in luring and selling boys and girls. The rented room was used as a hiding place for the abducted children. On the afternoon of the 18th, at 3 p.m., another woman, an accomplice of Wang and his wife, abducted Luo Xiaomao, a five-year-old boy, the son of Luo Jinru, the owner of Lichang Knitting Factory at No. 33 Xujiahui Road (east end of Belle Road) in the French Concession. The boy was handed over to Wang and his wife to be hidden at home. After losing his child, Luo Jinru sent people to search for him everywhere, but to no avail. That night, late at night, the child Luo Xiaomao cried incessantly because he was with strangers and missing his parents and family. Wang and his wife tried all kinds of coaxing, but it was ineffective. That night, the landlord, Yang Shuncai, and his family heard the child's crying and recognized the voice as that of Luo Jinru's son, Xiaomao, who had previously rented the front building. Because it was late at night, they didn't inquire about it but kept an eye on it. The next morning, they went upstairs to check on the child who had been crying the previous night and confirmed that it was Luo Xiaomao. Knowing that the child had been abducted, Yang Shuncai remained calm and secretly notified the child's parents and reported to the French police. Inspector Long Chenglong, Detective Zhang Ziying, Detective Dai Rongji, and others rushed to the address and arrested Wang Wu, along with the child she brought with her. The abducted child, Luo Xiaomao, was also rescued and returned to his family. Under interrogation, Wu confessed to abducting the child. Her husband, Wang Jiandong, had gone out early in the morning to buy clothing fabric to sew clothes for the abducted child and take him to another location for sale. Based on the confession, the police chief sent Detective Zhu Caicheng to wait at their residence. In less than ten minutes, the child trafficker Wang Jiandong returned home from outside, carrying a package of clothing fabric. He was immediately arrested and taken to the police station. Subsequently, three more accomplices, Li Wenqing, Lu Weng, and Cai Yucheng, were also apprehended and detained separately. Yesterday morning, the police transferred the five male and female defendants to the First Criminal Court of the Special First Court. Yuan Jiahuang, a lawyer from the Police Department, briefly presented the case, requesting a two-week postponement to conduct a detailed investigation and arrest the remaining accomplices, and requested a trial. Judge Xiong Hui Ping questioned the defendants, then adjourned the hearing to the 19th and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody.

Vocational Guidance Center Teaches and Helps Unemployed Youth 131

Pilot Program for a Chinese Goods Promotion Team: Recruiting Unemployed Youth to Serve as Salespeople

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center of the Chinese Vocational Education Society, recognizing the increasing number of unemployed people and the proliferation of imported goods, has organized a Chinese Goods Promotion Team. The program will be piloted for three months, and if it proves successful, it will be expanded to recruit unemployed youth to promote Chinese goods to households using specially marked rattan boxes containing domestically produced daily necessities from factories. Many Chinese goods manufacturers have supported this initiative by offering special discounts to make it easier for salespeople to sell their products, and for consumers to obtain daily necessities at lower-than-market prices without having to travel. It has been learned that the team has been organized and is headed by He Qingru and Pan Yangyao, as chairman and vice-chairman respectively. Ma Sicong Regularly Performs the Violin 132

First Public Performance in Shanghai of His Composed...Sonata

Ma Sicong, a world-renowned violinist and musician, will hold a violin recital at the Shanghai YMCA of the Eight Immortals Bridge on the evening of the 23rd of this month. Ma will publicly perform his Sonata (G major) for the first time. After graduating from the Paris National Conservatory of Music and returning to China, Ma received government funding in 1930 to return to France to study composition. He has made great achievements and has written many musical scores. It is reported that the sonata to be presented to the audience this time was composed in the spring of 1934. The entire piece is divided into three movements, and the form is classical. The first movement is a 3/4 time allegro, with several themes appearing in succession. After free modulation, the overall theme develops in the middle section and concludes in a lively manner after a recapitulation in G major chords. The overall theme of the second movement is a slow tempo in 5/8 time, followed by the violin playing a second theme in 2/4 time. The middle section includes a development of the transformed overall theme, followed by a recapitulation of the 5/8 time overall theme, concluding quietly. The third movement is a rapid rondo, with a very folk-song-like theme, ending brightly and resembling the first movement. It is reported that in addition to this sonata, Ma has also written a string quartet, a piano trio, a piano sonata, ancient-style songs, and other works.

Central Bank Inspection Report 136

Central Bank's 257th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Convertible Notes: "According to Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the issuance volume and reserve funds of the bank's convertible notes. The 257th inspection was conducted at the bank's issuing bureau on November 16th, 1935. The inspection results are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 144,193,402 silver dollars, including 131,072,922 silver dollar notes and 13,120,480 subsidiary coin notes. The total amount of convertible note reserve is 144,193,402 silver dollars, including 94,995,002 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 63,798,509.89 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuing vault, 1,020,000 silver dollars stored in the issuing branch, 2,576,929 silver dollars stored in various branches, and 27,599,562.11 silver dollars stored in fellow banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 49,198,400 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 586,679.80 customs gold units. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserve is 586,679.80 customs gold units. This reserve includes 11,553.59 taels of standard gold, which is equivalent to 586,679.80 customs gold units at a fixed price of 5.0779. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the remainder must be guaranteed by legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. November 18, 1935. Central Bank Supervisory Committee Chairman Li Fuxun, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyin."

Tan Zhuo Sues Father to Restore Father-Son Relationship 137

Father, Xiong Duyou, Remains Resolute; Lawyers' Mediation Difficult to Achieve

Tan Jingyu, a wealthy merchant from Guangdong, lives at No. 21, Fuan Lane, Hesker Road in this city. He made his fortune by operating real estate and amassed a vast fortune. He also has a considerable reputation in the business world. Mr. Tan has two sons, the eldest is named Tan Zhuo, who is 34 years old and lives at No. 63, Lane 427, Xiaoshadu Road, Wuding Road in this city. He serves as an associate at the Puyi Real Estate Company in this city. In 1921, when Tan Zhuo was just a young man, he discovered that his father, Jingyu, had improper conduct, which caused his father's displeasure. He was then expelled in anger and a public statement was published, declaring the severance of their father-son relationship. At that time, Tan Zhuo was so stimulated that he was determined to become strong. He was admitted to the Whampoa Military Academy. After graduation, he went to Germany for further study. After returning to China, he participated in the revolutionary work. In 1927, the Revolutionary Army launched the Northern Expedition, and he made some meritorious contributions. In 1930, he retired from the army and returned to Shanghai, where he worked at the Puyi Real Estate Company. However, considering that his father was old and worried about misunderstandings in the future and the duty of a son to serve, he requested to return home. However, Tan Jingyu still remembered the old hatred and refused in strong words. Tan Zhuo was forced to resort to law, but because it violated the principle of not suing twice for the same matter, his case was rejected by the court. He then appealed to the Supreme Court to confirm the father-son relationship. According to the Supreme Court's ruling No. 955 of 1934, Lawyers Chen Zhen and Liu Shichao filed a confirmation lawsuit with the local court. The court once approved the summons for trial, but the defendant did not appear in court. At 10 a.m. yesterday, Judge Zhu Run specially opened the Second Court for trial. The defendant, Tan Jingyu, still did not appear in court, but only entrusted a lawyer to appear in court as an agent. The plaintiff, Tan Zhuo, came to court with Lawyers Chen and Liu and testified: "I am 34 years old, a native of Zhongshan, Guangdong, living at No. 63, Lane 427, at the intersection of Xiaoshadu Road and Wuding Road. I request confirmation of inheritance and the elimination of interference with my rights. I am the defendant's legitimate eldest son. In July 1921, the defendant suspected that I had lost my integrity and published a statement declaring the severance of our father-son relationship. He also filed an employment case with the Shanghai Mixed Court. At that time, I thought that the defendant's statement severing the father-son relationship was a kind of disciplinary measure and that the nominal father-son relationship between us still existed. Therefore, since being expelled, I have studied hard for more than ten years. Later, I participated in the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army and made some meritorious contributions. In 1930, I retired from the army and returned to Shanghai. I repeatedly asked my father to return home to serve him and fulfill my filial duty, but he still remembered the old evils and did not allow it. I had no choice but to sue according to law." Then, the defendant's lawyer stated, "The defendant, Tan Jingyu, is 60 years old, a native of Zhongshan, Guangdong, living at No. 21, Anfu Lane, Hesker Road. He is unable to attend today due to illness. However, this lawyer has mediated several times, but the defendant has expressed his firm determination, making it difficult to approach him." The presiding judge then declared, "Fundamentally, there is no possibility of severing the father-son relationship. Therefore, the defendant's lawyer should be instructed to convey to the defendant that he must personally attend the next hearing for verification." Then the court adjourned.

Letter to the Editor 142

To the Editor: I have just read a news item in today's newspaper about the conclusion of the lawsuit between lawyers Lu Xingyuan and Qiu Hanping. There are some inaccuracies in it, such as the use of abusive language and the claim that he would have his hair shaved and made a prisoner, which are completely inconsistent with the facts. Mr. Xingyuan made a statement in court yesterday to state the plaintiff's intention, and of course, he presented various evidence and facts against the defendant, Qiu Hanping, attacking him for having no evidence and no excusable reason. This kind of attack is of course permitted by law, so what is the basis for saying that he was using abusive language? Furthermore, Mr. Xingyuan stated that Qiu Hanping had reported groundless accusations to the police and the court, requesting the detention of Mr. Xingyuan, Shi Zhinan, and Wang Dushi. If the authorities had mistakenly listened to him and immediately arrested them, Mr. Xingyuan and others would have suffered unexpected insults and serious damages, or if the court of first instance had wrongly convicted and sentenced them, they would have been detained in the Western Jail and had their hair shaved. Even if they were acquitted, there would be no compensation for the unjust imprisonment. The trend of false accusations should not be allowed to continue. Finally, based on the documentary evidence presented in court, Qiu Hanping had committed a criminal act and should be punished with the crime he deserved, without probation, in order to deter others. This is the actual situation that day. I should like to request that your newspaper reproduce this letter for correction, for the sake of public justice. Sincerely, Lawyer Lu Xingyuan, November 20th.

Incoming Correspondence: The Path to Political Reform (Continued) 145

— Shen Gongzhan (November of the 24th year in Shanghai)

——Respectfully dedicated to the comrades of the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Nationalist Party and gentlemen who are interested in discussing political reform—

(6) The President should be considered the head of government who controls the "governing power". Therefore, the clause in the original draft constitution that "the President exercises executive power" should be amended to "the President exercises governing power", so that it is in line with the spirit of the Five-Power Constitution's creation of separately defined "powers". Therefore, the presidents of the five Yuan can all be nominated by the President and appointed with the consent of the National Assembly, rather than being elected by the National Assembly. As for the members of the Legislative Yuan and the Control Yuan, the presidents of the Legislative Yuan and the Control Yuan can nominate candidates separately according to the population ratio of each region, not limited to the representatives of the National Assembly (at least more than half should be members of the Nationalist Party), and submit them to the President for approval and then to the National Assembly for approval before appointing them. In this way, even if the National Assembly is adjourned, there will still be a portion of national representatives able to participate in the work of legislation and supervision. In addition, if the Legislative Yuan or the Control Yuan's duties involve any powers within a certain regime, they should be included in the duties of the National Assembly, or at least submitted to the National Assembly or

the Provisional National Assembly for approval before they can take effect, in order to clarify the boundaries of power.

(C) Regarding the organizers of the Party:

(1) The internal organization of the Nationalist Party should be made even more rigorous. In addition to the Premier, there should be a Director-General (or Leader) who has overall command of the Party. In addition to the Director-General, a Central Executive Committee should be established as the organ for deciding the Party's program and policies. The Director-General has the power of final decision and is responsible for guiding its implementation.

(2) The Central Party Headquarters should be as active as possible, taking control of the core of the National Assembly. Other party headquarters at all levels should also be as active as possible, taking control of the core of local parliamentary and consultative bodies.

(3) The executive organs of provincial or special municipal party headquarters should change from an election system to a special appointment system, with one to three commissioners appointed by the Central Party Headquarters to preside over them. The supervisory organs should still be elected by each level.

(4) Whether to establish county or district party headquarters should be determined by each province or municipality, taking into account local conditions and submitting proposals to the Central Government for approval. (End)

Overview of the Shanghai Woolen Industry (Continued) 146

— Edited by the China Credit Information Service

(Two of the Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

The Shanghai woolen industry has entered the second stage from the first stage. The performance in terms of woolen imports is the sudden decrease in the amount (only imported more than one million customs gold units in the first nine months of this year). The performance in terms of wool imports, on the contrary, is the sharp increase in the amount, increasing from 931,461 customs gold units in the 22nd year to 2,816,084 customs gold units in the 23rd year. (Because wool raw materials need to be imported six months or one year in advance) One decrease and one increase is the most worthy of consideration. We should realize that if we want to remedy the past leak of the woolen industry, we must pay close attention to animal husbandry in the Northwest. 2. Overview of Shanghai's Chinese and Foreign Woolen Factories

The manufacturing of woolens in Shanghai is a new phenomenon in recent years, which can be divided into two types. One is specialized manufacturing, such as Shanghai China Bodeyun and other factories, and the other is part-time manufacturing, such as the former Zhenxing and Zhanghua factories, which spun woolens in addition to woolen fabrics. Another example is the Yihe and Shanghai Textile factories, which are engaged in cotton textile industry and also manufacture woolens. The situation of the main factories is recorded separately as follows.

1. Yumin Textile Company

Yumin Textile Company was jointly established by the woolen shops on Xingsheng Street in the French Concession. It was established in September last year with a capital of 100,000 national currency. The address is on the Rong Maochang Building at No. 43 Xingsheng Street, French Concession, Shanghai. There is no separate factory. The Shuangyang brand and Shuangshou brand woolens are all manufactured by Anle Cotton Wool Weaving Factory on Bailinan Road. The wool required is purchased from Australia by Deki Lixing and Yihua companies.

2. Shanghai Woolen Textile Factory

Shanghai Woolen Textile Factory was jointly established by Wang Qiyu, Yu Zuoting, Guo Shun and other magnates. It was established in October last year with a capital of 150,000 yuan. The general issuing office is located at No. 349 Ningbo Road, and the factory is located at No. 61 Yangshupu Road. It specializes in spinning woolens, mostly four-strand velvet. It can produce 1,500 pounds per day. Its trademark is Xiaonan. Other Golden Dog, Double Cat, and Double species have not yet been started. There are more than a dozen machines in the factory, with 600 woolen spindles. Including other auxiliary machines, the total value is about 100,000 yuan. More than hundreds of workers are employed, mostly female workers.

3. China Woolen Textile Factory

The China Woolen Textile Factory is different from Yumin and Shanghai. It is independently operated by Chen Zhilian, a native of Lianxing, Zhejiang, with a capital of about 1.5 million yuan. It started manufacturing in July of this year. The factory is located at No. 188 Jianqing Road, covering an area of more than twelve mu. Its machines are ordered from French manufacturers by Dewey Foreign Company. There are two warping machines, one doubling machine, eight drawing machines, five spindle machines, and zero-component motors, etc., worth about 200,000 yuan. About five or sixty workers are employed. The Queen brand woolen, which has suddenly emerged in the market, is its product.

4. Bodeyun Woolen Thread Factory

Shanghai Bodeyun Woolen Thread Factory is a branch of the parent factory in England. Its head office and factory are located north of Dinghai Bridge on Poyang Road, and the business office is located at No. 2 Beijing Road. The capital is about 10 million Chinese currency. The factory building was completed at the end of last year, and officially started production in March of this year. It can produce one British pound of velvet thread per day. A total of more than 600 male and female workers are employed. In addition to the well-known Bee brand, the products also include Azalea and Parrot brands.

The above four are newly emerging factories specializing in the manufacture of woolens. In addition, the British-owned Yihua Yarn Factory also produces Five Blessings brand woolens, and the Japanese-owned Shanghai Yarn Factory also produces non-branded woolens, which are mixed and sold on the market. Since they are not specialized operations, they are not described in detail. The latest market prices of woolens produced by each factory are listed below for comparison. (Unit: yuan)

Factory Name Woolen Brand Wholesale Price Retail Price

Bodeyun Bee 2.90 3.20

Bodeyun Azalea 1.50 ——

Yumin Double Hand 1.70 2.40

Shanghai Xiaonan 1.50 1.90

China Queen 3.00 3.30

Yihua Five Blessings 0.80 ——

Shanghai Yarn Factory No Brand 2.50 ——

Generally speaking, due to competition and sluggish sales, the market price of woolens this year is slightly lower than last year. However, since the implementation of the new currency policy recently, the price of imported wool has been expensive, and the market prices of various brands have turned upward again.

Yumin's Sheep brand and Shanghai's Xiaonan brand once dropped prices to compete for sales, and both sides were considerably affected. However, in September of this year, Yumin Company ordered 200 packages of Xiaonan brand from Shanghai Woolen Textile Factory, and the two sides have the intention of starting cooperation, which is really good news for Chinese businesses to cooperate to resist foreign aggression. The Bee brand produced by Bodeyun has a long history and its promotion power is also great, making it a formidable competitor for Chinese businesses. What is somewhat comforting is that its sales are mainly limited to South China, while Chinese businesses are biased towards North China, which may not be directly opposed. In short, whether the national woolen industry can continue to develop in the future depends on the one hand on the rectification and prosperity of the domestic political economy, and on the other hand on the ability to cope with external pressures.

Ma Junwu Discusses New Facilities at Guangxi University 149

Most Graduates Can Find Jobs in the Province

Guangxi Province Promotes Compulsory Education Very Hard

(Special dispatch from Beiping) Ma Junwu, the president of Guangxi University, came to Peiping from Shanghai a few days ago to visit various friends. At 11 am on the 19th, the reporter went to Bai Pengfei's private residence, the president of the Faculty of Law and Commerce of Peiping University, to visit Ma (Ma lives in Bai's house) to inquire about the recent situation of Guangxi University and the development of compulsory education teachers and vocational education teachers in the province in recent years. Ma made the following statement: Guangxi University was founded in the 17th year of the Republic of China. The campus is located in Wuzhou. It is divided into three colleges: science, agriculture, and engineering. There are no colleges of liberal arts or law. The main reason is that there are many young people in Guangxi studying in other provinces who specialize in liberal arts and law, and there is a lack of personnel in science, agriculture, and engineering. There are currently more than 800 students in the school, including only more than 60 female students. The College of Science has four departments: mathematics, physics, chemistry, and biology. The dean is Duan Zixie. The College of Agriculture has two departments: agriculture and forestry. The dean is He Zhuqi. The College of Engineering has four departments: mechanical engineering, civil engineering, mining, and metallurgy. The dean is Jin Xiru. There are more than 100 faculty members. The faculty are all full-time, and the remuneration is the same as that of other universities in China. At the beginning of its establishment, the cost of equipment was about 1 million yuan. Therefore, in terms of equipment, such as the library, science laboratory, factory and farm, student dormitories, and auditorium, it can still be used. The annual recurring expenses are 400,000 yuan, which is directly allocated by the Guangxi Provincial Government. Faculty salaries account for about two-thirds, and equipment and book expenses account for about one-quarter. It is still difficult to talk about whether to add colleges of liberal arts, law, and medicine in the future. In recent years, industry and construction in Guangxi Province have made rapid progress, so most of the graduates of our school serve in the province. As for the recent promotion of compulsory education and vocational education in Guangxi Province, great efforts have also been made to gradually reduce illiteracy. However, the funding is not very sufficient, which is an obstacle to development. I (Ma refers to himself) took the opportunity of going to Beijing to report on school affairs to the Ministry of Education and came to Peiping to visit various friends. I will leave Peiping for Kaifeng on the 22nd to attend the engineering college of Henan University and give a lecture. After a short stay, I will go to Wuhan and then to Shanghai to return to Guangxi.

Ministry of Education Solicits Self-Compiled Lecture Notes for Various Vocational School Subjects 150

The Ministry of Education stated that vocational schools have a wide variety of subjects, and it is not easy to determine the standards for each subject's curriculum. The Ministry has already issued a letter to outstanding vocational schools and experts in various subjects in China, requesting them to draft course schedules and teaching material outlines for each subject, compile them into four volumes, and distribute them to various schools for reference. It is now found that vocational schools often edit their own lecture notes when selecting teaching materials for each subject, but the content varies in detail, and each has its own strengths and weaknesses, which urgently need to be improved. Therefore, the Ministry has specially solicited self-compiled lecture notes from public and private vocational schools that have been running for a long time or have achieved results, and will review them so that they can be adopted by various schools to improve them. It is appropriate to list the names of various schools and order the bureau to quickly forward the order to the schools to select self-compiled lecture notes or practical teaching materials for various vocational subjects that have been used for a considerable period of time and are considered suitable for application, and send them to the Ministry by a specified date for review. In addition, if the textbooks for each subject selected by the schools are considered to be suitable for the level and can be used for teaching, they should also indicate the publisher and the name of the editor of the book, and list them together and send them to the Ministry. The Education Department Promises to Negotiate with the Finance Department

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (101) 157

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"We all need these small helps; so you must try to learn your lessons and work hard, play with the children in a kind way, and make good use of your holidays; if you can give me an excellent report, or although I don't say it, I have already seen it and know it, because I am very good at detecting all the good efforts of my children—then you can win a drawer in which to put your treasures. You see, some drawers have already been divided into four small parts, and I will order other drawers to be done in the same way, each part for one week; when that drawer is full of precious and beautiful things, I will be as proud as you are, I think even more proud—because in those pebbles, moss, and beautiful butterflies, I will see the thorough implementation of good will, the self-control of mistakes, and the fulfillment of promises. Shall we do this, Don?"

The boy didn't say a word, just looked at her, but his expression showed that he deeply felt and understood her words and wishes, but he didn't know how to express his gratitude for that kind of love and kindness: she also understood that kind of expression, and seeing his face flushed, knew that he was indeed moved—which was exactly what she hoped for—she then stopped saying a word about that brand new plan, but took out the highest drawer, brushed off the dust, and placed it on two chairs in front of the sofa, and hurriedly said:

"Now, let's immediately start putting those interesting hard-shelled insects in a safe place. These grids can hold many things, you see. I will nail the butterflies and insects on the four sides; this way they are very safe, leaving the bottom to place larger pieces. I will give you some raw cotton, clean paper, and pins, so you can prepare for this week's work."

"But I can't go out to find new things," Don said, looking at his feet, showing a pitiful look.

Yesterday's Friendly Football Match: St. John's Defeats Jiaotong Again 158

Xu Wenkui and Zhu Wenji Perform Excellently; Jiaotong Lacks Coordination and Strength, Zhou Guangzhong Struggles to Support the Entire Team

The St. John's University football team, possessing many strong players, has recently added Xu Chengxun, the Fujian representative from the current National Games, further strengthening its power. In yesterday's match against Jiaotong University, Jiaotong was overwhelmed. Xu Wenkui, Zhu Wenji, and others delivered outstanding performances. Jiaotong appeared weak and disorganized; Xue Wenxiu and Zhou Guangzhong struggled to carry the team. As a result, Jiaotong lost to St. John's again with a score of 3-1.

First Half: 2-1

At 3:30 PM, the referee, Mr. Bibei'er, blew the silver whistle, and the two teams lined up to compete. Jiaotong took the initial offensive, displaying great momentum. St. John's Xu Guangyao, in his eagerness to save the ball, carelessly touched it with his hand, resulting in a penalty kick. Shao Jihua took the penalty, sending the ball into the upper left corner, opening the scoring. St. John's then launched a vigorous attack. Zhu Wenji initiated an offensive from the flank, reaching an opportune spot and passing it to the center. Xu Wenkui received the ball, unleashed a powerful shot, and scored, leveling the score at 1-1. After the kickoff from the center line, Zhou Guangzhong received the ball and sent it far to Wenxiu. However, Wenxiu was too eager for victory and shot too high, returning empty-handed. St. John's Li Guangxing dribbled the ball forward, passing it to Zhu Wenji. Wenji dared not delay, forcefully kicking the ball towards Jiaotong's goal. Cheng Guoyin kicked it away, but not far enough. Fan Jiaju rushed forward to save the situation, but Zhu Wenji seized the opportunity, lightly tapping the ball, which went into the net again. Afterwards, the ball often hovered around Jiaotong's goal, fortunately Jiaju was agile and saved many dangerous shots. As a result, St. John's took the lead in the first half with a score of 2-1.

Second Half: 1-0

After the break, St. John's introduced fresh players, while Jiaotong retained the same lineup. The fighting became very loose, and the kicking lacked strength. The defense appeared weak, with repeated mistakes. Although Zhou Guangzhong ran all over the field, it was of no use. St. John's, however, grew stronger as the game progressed. Xu Chengxun shot directly at the goal from 30 yards, quickly and powerfully, but unfortunately missed. Zhu Wenji, seeing this, became even more determined to fight hard. Fan Jiaju calmly made two touches, and the ball bounced out. Jiaotong found it difficult to recover and lacked the strength. Xue Wenxiu missed two more opportunities, achieving nothing. St. John's Chen Ji'en advanced from the right, intending to pass it to the center, but without support, he shot directly at the goal, scoring successfully. This shot was clear and beautiful. From then on, both teams traded attacks, but neither team scored again. In the second half, St. John's won again with a score of 1-0. As a result, Jiaotong lost again with a score of 3-1. The lineups of both sides are as follows:
